Julmonzhae Moore 
August 29, 2023 
054658453-02
The following is a settlement demand on behalf of our client, Julmonzhae Moore (“Ms. Moore” 
or “our client”), for the injuries she sustained on August 29, 2023, when Ms. Moore was injured 
an incident involving Naomi Robinson (“Ms. Robinson” or “your insured”). 
This demand is prepared in an attempt to resolve our client’s claim and is a privileged settlement 
communication under Ind. R. Evid. 408. This demand is not intended for use in future litigation 
without our consent. No information contained herein should be considered a factual or legal 
admission by our client.
We expect that you will provide us with a list of any additional items you need to fully evaluate 
this demand within 15 days of the date of this letter. We will respond to any requests you make 
for additional information forthwith. We also ask that this demand be immediately forwarded
to all insurance company decision-makers and, of course, the insured policyholder.
1. FACTS & LIABILITY

2
On August 29, 2023, Ms. Moore was the restrained rear-seat passenger of a vehicle (“Unit 2”) 
operated by Dewayne Ward (“Mr. Ward”) traveling southbound on Charlestown Road near its 
intersection with the Interstate Highway 265 entrance ramp in New Albany, Floyd County, 
Indiana. At the same time, Ms. Robinson was the driver of a vehicle (“Unit 1”) traveling 
northbound on Charlestown Road, near the same intersection. As Mr. Ward lawfully turned left 
onto the Interstate Highway 265 entrance ramp on a green light, suddenly and without warning, 
Ms. Robinson failed to yield to the right of way, and the front of her vehicle violently collided 
with the front passenger side of Mr. Ward’s vehicle. The force of the impact caused Mr. Ward’s 
vehicle to spin around and it came to a rest facing north on Charlestown Road. Upon impact, Ms. 
Moore’s side airbags were immediately deployed, and her body was violently jolted around the 
interior of the vehicle. Ms. Moore was transported by EMS to the ULH University of Louisville 
Hospital. The collision resulted in Ms. Moore sustaining significant personal injuries and other
damages.
As exposed in the Indiana Officer’s Standard Crash Report,1 Officer Noah Stone of the New 
Albany Police Department investigated the collision.
1 Exhibit 1 - Indiana Officer’s Standard Crash Report
NotTo
Scale

3
The conditions for establishing liability, in this case, are clear. Ms. Robinson owed a duty of 
care to the other drivers on the road. Pursuant to IN Code § 9-21-5-1(a), “[a] person may not drive 
a vehicle on a highway at a speed greater than is reasonable and prudent under the conditions, 
having regard to the actual and potential hazards then existing. Speed shall be restricted as 
necessary to avoid colliding with a person, vehicle, or other conveyance on, near, or entering a 
highway in compliance with legal requirements and with the duty of all persons to use due care.” 
Furthermore, pursuant to IN Code § 9-21-5-4(a), “[t]he driver of each vehicle shall, consistent 
with section 1 of this chapter, drive at an appropriate reduced speed as follows: (1) When 
approaching and crossing an intersection or railway grade crossing…”
On the date of loss, Ms. Robinson lacked attentiveness, failed to yield to the right of way, operated 
her vehicle at an excessive rate of speed for traffic conditions, failed to keep a proper lookout, and 
caused a collision with the vehicle that Ms. Moore was traveling in. As a result of Ms. Robinson’s 
acts and/or omissions on August 29, 2023, Ms. Moore suffered significant personal injuries and 
damages for which Ms. Robinson is undoubtedly liable.
2. SUMMARY OF INJURIES
We have enclosed all pertinent medical information regarding Ms. Moore’s injuries. These injuries 
were suffered as a direct and proximate result of this incident. The chart below represents a nonexhaustive summary of the injuries sustained by our client:

If you claim any of the medical treatment was unnecessary or any of the bills were unreasonable, 
please identify in writing which bills you dispute and the factual basis for such dispute. If you 
dispute them with a qualified expert opinion from a doctor willing to testify, then please provide 
us with a copy of his or her report. If not, please confirm in writing that you dispute the bills as a 
claims adjuster and/or administrator and not as a qualified medical professional. If you do not 
respond in writing as requested, we will assume you do not dispute the amount of medical bills set 
forth within this demand package.
3.3. Future Medical Expenses
Ms. Moore continues to experience pain and symptomatology as a result of the injuries she 
sustained in the incident at issue and will require additional treatment moving forward, including, 
but not limited to, chiropractic treatment. Thus, a conservative estimate of future medical care for 
Ms. Moore is $9,360.00.
Procedure Years Per Year Cost Total
Chiropractic 
Treatment2
3 6 $520.00 $9,360.00
Total $9,360.00
Note that the costs of healthcare and medication will continue to rise significantly, and we reserve 
the right to revise our projection of future medicals on this basis, among others. We also note that 
this estimate is only for one year and could readily be augmented for additional years of healthcare 
and medication.
3.4. Past and Future Pain and Suffering
Under Indiana law, historically, the most highly compensable area of damages, in general, is in 
the area of physical pain and suffering.
There is no question that the August 29, 2023, incident caused Ms. Moore a great deal of physical 
and emotional pain and suffering. As a result of the incident, Ms. Moore suffered serious injuries 
2
Starlite Chiropractic - Bills

6
that affected, and continue to affect, her quality of life. Ms. Moore experienced difficulty and pain 
when trying to complete simple daily activities that she used to be able to complete with ease prior 
to the August 29, 2023, incident. To this day, Ms. Moore continues to experience pain and 
discomfort as a result of the August 29, 2023, incident at issue. 
Ms. Moore’s pain and suffering as a result of the August 29, 2023, incident should remain at the 
forefront of your consideration as you evaluate her significant noneconomic damages.
Per Diem Analysis
Our conservative per diem analysis shows that Ms. Moore’s claim for past, present, and future 
pain and suffering is valued at $107,072.00. A jury will consider not only Ms. Moore’s initial pain 
and suffering to date, but also her subsequent pain and suffering. Below are some very conservative 
figures we would present to a jury to consider, in addition to her other damages:
● $25.00/hr. for initial pain and suffering from August 29, 2023, to November 29, 2023; and
● $12.00/hr. for subsequent pain and suffering from November 29, 2023, to November 29, 
2024.
Pain & Suffering

Total Pain and Suffering $107,072.00
In light of the per diem analysis above, we assert that $107,072.00 is fair and equitable 
compensation for Ms. Moore’s initial and subsequent pain and suffering.

7
4. DEMAND TO SETTLE
We believe that the above evaluation is a fair and reasonable calculation of our client’s damages. 
As you will note, our client’s economic and non-economic damages total at least $145,171.40. Our 
client will settle her claim for a minimum of the policy limits.
If a software product is being used to generate payout ranges as to this claim, we request that you 
communicate the range of results generated by your software.
Please respond within 15 days of receipt of this demand. If the terms of this demand are not 
accepted, we have been authorized by our client to promptly file suit. Please feel free to contact 
me should you have any questions. 
 
Sincerely,
Aaron G. Whaley, Esq
Aaron G. Whaley, Esq.

The following was written by STONE, NOAH
On Tuesday, August 29, 2023 at 8:40 P.M., Officer Stone responded to a crash on Charlestown Road at intersection the of |-265 E. The
weather was clear and the road surface was dry.
Vehicle 1, Black Chevrolet Malibu, Going straight.
Vehicle 2, Black Kia Optima, Turning left.
Upon arrival to crash scene | observed Vehicle 2 to be facing Northbound on Charlestown Road, and Vehicle 1 in the grass area to the East
of Charlestown Road. | observed Driver 1 laying on the ground with the complaint of back and neck pain, 1 passenger of vehicle 2 sitting in
the grass with the complaint of head pain and stated she was not wearing a seat belt, and 1 passenger of vehicle 2 on the ground having a
seizure. Driver 2 had the complaint of pain coming from their right ribs and left knee, and refused medical treatment. 1 passenger of vehicle 2
had the complaint of pain coming from their face and refused medical treatment.
Driver 1 and 2 passengers of vehicle 2 were transported to the University of Louisville Hospital.
On scene, Driver 2 stated that he was in the left turn lane Southbound on Charlestown Road, with a green light turning left. Driver 2 stated
that Vehicle 1 crashed into the front passenger side of Vehicle 2 while Vehicle 2 was turning left. ECM
| contacted Driver 1 on August 30, 2023, at approximately 1:34 P.M. Driver 1 stated that they were driving Northbound on Charlestown Road.
Driver 1 advised they were going through the intersection of Charlestown Road and |-265 E, and that Driver 1 had a yellow light.
Both vehicles were towed by Bennetts Towing to Bennetts Towing lot.

Basic Information
 
Transfer of care addendum: Transfer of care from Dr. HILL NORBY. Please refer to that documentation for complete history and
physical exam. Please refer to this documentation for final disposition unless otherwise specified below.
 
Briefly: Patient is a 19 year old female with no PMHx who presents to room 9 following a MVA. Patient was an unrestrained backseat
passenger involved in a head on collision. Patient complained of shoulder and belly pain. Man scan is negative. Patient is pending
right shoulder x-ray.
 
Right shoulder x-rays negative for any acute fracture or dislocation. I spoke with the patient regarding her labs and imaging results.
We will treat her pain with a short course of NSAIDs as well as muscle relaxers. She was given strict return precautions. She was
able to tolerate p.o. in the emergency department and able to ambulate without assistance. Advised to follow-up with her primary
care provider and discharged home.

Basic Information
Patient information:.
History of Present Illness
Patient is a 19 year old female with no significant PMHx who presents to the ED via EMS following a MVA. Patient was an unrestrained back seat
passenger. The vehicles collided head on but the speed of each vehicle is unknown. Airbags deployed. LOC is unknown but patient was ambulatory on
scene. Patient complains of pain in her head, stomach, and right shoulder. She rates her pain 8/10.
 
Room 9 Interventions:
Attending Dr. Ross present and available throughout
Pt brought to Room 9 by EMS
EMS notification was not given PTA
Connected to O2, cardiac, BP, pulse ox monitor
Primary survey:
- Airway: intact
- Breathing: bilateral breath sounds
- Circulation: 2+ pulses in all 4 extremities
Transferred to Room 9 Bed where brief initial survey showed: Please see physical exam below
Interventions PTA: put on 2L O2 NC
Interventions in Room 9: none
Consults: none
Impression: mva
Disposition: ct
Critical care time excluding procedures: 11 minutes.
 
21:29 - arrival
21:31 - 122/78 manual bp
21:40 - transfer to CT
 
Physical Examination
 
Vital Signs
Per nurse's notes.
General: Alert, no acute distress.
Skin: Warm, dry.
Head: Normocephalic, atraumatic.
Neck: Trachea midline, no tenderness.
Eye: Pupils are equal, round and reactive to light, extraocular movements are intact, vision unchanged, pupils 3 equal.
Ears, nose, mouth and throat: No hemotympanum.
Cardiovascular: Regular rate and rhythm, Normal peripheral perfusion.
Respiratory: Lungs are clear to auscultation, respirations are non-labored, BS equal bilaterally, Symmetrical chest wall expansion.
Chest wall: No tenderness, No deformity, No seatbelt sign.

Medical Decision Making
Patient presents after MVA. ABCs intact on arrival and secondary survey most notable for headache, R shoulder pain, and back pain. DDx to include
ICH, other intrathoracic injury including pneumo/hemo-, intra-abdominal bleed, fracture, dislocation. Patient was initiated on IV fluids. Pain managed as
needed and patient stable for CT scanner. Upon review of CT imaging patient noted to have no intracranial injury, cervical/thoracic/lumbar spine injury.
There was no intrathoracic or intra-abdominal injury noted as well. Lab work reviewed and notable for electrolytes within normal limits, creatinine of 0.7,
with WBC of 10 and patient's hemoglobin stable at 12. Pending plain film of the right shoulder, TOC to Dr. Adam. I suspect this patient will be
appropriate for discharge upon completion of this x-ray however please refer to his documentation for any additional care provided prior to discharge.

Take your medications faithfully. Do NOT skip medication. Do NOT stop taking medications without the direction of a health care
provider. Carry a list of your medications with you at all times, and take this medication list with you to your first follow up visit. Report

As part of your treatment plan, your provider may have prescribed a limited course of a controlled substance. This medication may be
given to help people with moderate or severe pain or for other medical conditions, but there are risks involved with treatment. Common
side effects may include nausea, constipation, drowsiness, sweating, itching, dry mouth, and rash. More serious side effects may
include cognitive and motor impairment, like problems with thinking, concentrating, alertness, and movement (e.g. slowed reflexes), and
driving and operating heavy machinery can be dangerous. It is important for you to talk to your provider if you have these side effects or
questions. These controlled substances can produce physical dependence and be habit-forming if taken for an extended period of time,
which means that the body has gotten used to them and may experience withdrawal symptoms, if they are abruptly stopped. Withdrawal
symptoms can include runny nose, sweating, goose bumps, diarrhea, abdominal cramping, rapid heartbeat, difficulty sleeping, and
nervousness. Please dispose of unused and expired medications per pharmacy guidance.

Emergency
Education Materials
RICE Therapy for Routine Care of Injuries
The routine care of many injuries includes rest, ice, compression, and elevation (RICE therapy). RICE therapy is often recommended for
injuries to soft tissues, such as muscle strain, sprains, bruises, and overuse injuries. It can also be used for some bone injuries. Using
RICE therapy can help to relieve pain and lessen swelling.
Supplies needed:
• Ice.
• Plastic bag.
• Towel.
• Elastic bandage.
• Pillow or pillows to raise (elevate) the injured body part.
How to care for your injury with RICE therapy
Rest
Rest your injury. This may help with the healing process. Rest usually involves limiting your normal activities and not using the injured
part of your body. Generally, you can return to your normal activities when your health care provider says it is okay and you can do them
without much discomfort.
If you rest the injury too much, it may not heal as well. Some injuries heal better with early movement instead of resting for too long. Talk
with your health care provider about how you should limit your activities and whether you should start range-of-motion exercises for your
injury.
Ice
Ice your injury to lessen swelling and pain. Do not apply ice directly to your skin.
• Put ice in a plastic bag.
• Place a towel between your skin and the bag.
Page 25 of 118
ULH University of Louisville Hospital

Report Request ID: 192370939 10/2/2023 12:00 EDT
Emergency
• Leave the ice on for 20 minutes, 2–3 times a day. Use ice on as many days as told by your health care provider.
Compression
Put pressure (compression) on your injured area to control swelling, give support, and help with discomfort. Compression may be done
with an elastic bandage. If an elastic bandage has been applied, follow these general tips:
• Use the bandage as directed by the maker of the bandage that you are using.
• Do not wrap the bandage too tightly. That may block (cut off) circulation in the arm or leg in the area below the bandage.
—46 If part of your body beyond the bandage becomes blue, numb, cold, swollen, or more painful, your bandage is
probably too tight. If this occurs, remove your bandage and reapply it more loosely.
• Remove and reapply the bandage every 3–4 hours or as told by your health care provider.
• See your health care provider if the bandage seems to be making your problems worse rather than better.
Elevation
Elevate your injured area to lessen swelling and pain. If possible, elevate your injured area at or above the level of your heart or the
center of your chest.
Contact a health care provider if:
• Your pain and swelling continue.
• Your symptoms are getting worse rather than improving.
Having these problems may mean that you need further evaluation or imaging tests, such as X-rays or an MRI. Sometimes, X-rays may
not show a small broken bone (fracture) until days after the injury happened. Make a follow-up appointment with your health care
provider. Ask your health care provider, or the department that is doing the imaging test, when your results will be ready.
Get help right away if:
• You have sudden severe pain at or below the area of your injury.
• You have redness or increased swelling around your injury.
• You have tingling or numbness at or below the area of your injury and it does not improve after you remove the elastic
bandage.
Summary

Emergency Awareness and Preventative Care
STROKE is an EMERGENCY
Every Minute Counts
Act FAST and Check for these signs:
FACE Does the face look uneven?
ARM Does one arm drift down?
SPEECH Does their speech sound
strange?
TIME Call 9-1-1 at any sign of stroke
Stroke Risk Factors
Atrial Fibrillation
(irregular heartbeat) Diabetes Family history ofstroke
Heart Disease Heavy alcohol use High Blood Pressure
High Cholesterol Physical inactivity
and obesity Smoking
Cigarette Smoking
The facts are clear, cigarette smoking will shorten your life. Smoking can cause many illnesses along the way. As a healthcare provider,
we recommend that you stop smoking. Assistance with quitting is available by contacting 1-800-QUIT-NOW. This is a free resource
providing counseling, support, and referral. Or you may contact your personal physician.
988 Suicide & Crisis Lifeline: 988
The 988 Suicide & Crisis Lifeline is a national network of local crisis centers that provides free and confidential emotional support to
people in suicidal crisis or emotional distress 24 hours a day, 7 days a week. 
Don't Wait! Stop a Heart Attack Before It Starts
What is a heart attack?
A heart attack is damage or death to a part of the heart from severely decreased or lack of blood flow to the heart. Over time, arteries
can become narrow from the buildup of fat and cholesterol, which is called plaque. The plaque can rupture causing a blood clot to form.
When the blood clot forms, the artery can become severely narrowed or completely blocked, causing a heart attack.

• Heart attack is the leading cause of death in the United States.
• 85% of muscle damage occurs within the first 2 hours.
• Delay in the recognition of heart attack symptoms increases the chances of death.
Know the early symptoms of a heart attack:
Nausea
Feeling of
"fullness" in
chest
Jaw Pain
Pain that travels
down one or
both arms
Fatigue/being
tired Anxiety Back Pain
Chest pressure,
squeezing, or
discomfort

breath
Sweating, or a
cold sweat
Feeling of
impending
doom
There are unusual signs of heart attack, too!
Women, the elderly, and diabetics may present with atypical symptoms:
• Fainting/dizziness
• Weakness
• Confusion
Risk Factors for a Heart Attack
Some heart disease risk factors, such as age and family, cannot be changed. Others, like smoking and lack of exercise, can be
changed.
Smoking High Cholesterol Blood Pressure
Family History Obesity Age
Gender (Males are
at higher risk) Lack of Exercise Diabetes
Diet Stress Excessive Alcohol
Intake
If you or someone you know is experiencing the signs and symptoms of a heart attack, DON'T DELAY.
Call 9-1-1 immediately and seek help.
If someone collapses, perform CPR!
Do not attempt to drive if you are having symptoms of heart attack.
Why Hands-Only CPR?
• Hands-Only CPR has been shown to be as effective as conventional CPR for cardiac arrests that occur outside of a hospital.
• Survival depends on immediately receiving CPR from someone nearby.
How do you perform Hands-Only CPR?
There are two easy steps:

Save a life!
4 WAYS TO GET AHEAD OF SEPSIS
SEPSIS is a MEDICAL EMERGENCY. Time Matters!
Infections put you and your family at risk for a life-threatening condition called sepsis.
• Sepsis is the body's extreme response to an infection. It is life-threatening, and without timely treatment, sepsis can rapidly lead
to tissue damage, organ failure, and death. Sepsis happens when an infection you already have-in your skin, lungs, urinary tract
or somewhere else-riggers a chain reaction throughout your body.
1
PREVENT
INFECTIONS
• Take good care of
chronic conditions.
• Talk to your doctor
about getting the
recommended
vaccines.
2
PRACTICE GOOD
HYGIENE
• Wash your hands
frequently.
• Keep cuts or open
sores clean and
covered until they
are healed.
3
KNOW THE
SYMPTOMS
• Confusion or
disorientation
• Shortness of breath
• High heart rate
• Fever, shivering, or
feeling very cold
• Extreme pain or
discomfort
• Clammy or sweaty
skin
4 ACT FAST
• Get medical care
IMMEDIATELY if
you suspect sepsis
or if you have an
infection that is not
getting better or is
getting worse.
To learn more about sepsis and how to prevent infections, visit www.cdc.gov/sepsis.

The examination and treatment you have received in the Emergency Department has been done to provide an appropriate evaluation
and stabilizing treatment on an emergency basis only. Given the limited resources, it is not meant to be a substitute for complete
medical care. The follow-up provider you named will receive a copy of your records and all test reports. IT IS IMPORTANT THAT YOU
SCHEDULE A FOLLOW-UP APPOINTMENT AND BE RE-EVALUATED. You should report any new complaints, symptoms, or
remaining problems at that time. IT IS IMPOSSIBLE FOR THE EMERGENCY DEPARTMENT TO RECOGNIZE AND TREAT ALL
ELEMENTS OF INJURY OR ILLNESS IN A SINGLE VISIT.
If you have been referred to a specialist provider, it means that we believe you may have a condition that requires the expertise of a
specialist. These providers work in partnership with the hospital and have agreed to see referred patients in their office for further
evaluation. KEEP IN MIND THAT THE SPECIALIST HAS HIS/HER OWN OFFICE POLICIES WHICH MAY REQUIRE PROPER
INSURANCE OR PAYMENT UP FRONT BEFORE THE SPECIALIST WILL SEE YOU. It is your responsibility to call the specialist
provider to make an appointment. We do not have the ability to refer patients to specialists/physicians that work with specific insurance
companies.
Please be advised that all financial charges or billing practices are determined by that practice, not the hospital. If your insurance
company requires that you see a specialist from their approved list, it is your responsibility to contact your insurance company to make
those arrangements. It is also your responsibility to follow any other requirements of your insurance company necessary to obtain
coverage for claims submitted.
I hereby acknowledge receipt of these instructions and information above. I understand that I have received Emergency Treatment only,
which is not a substitute for complete medical care and acknowledge that all of my medical problems may not be known, identified, or
treated prior to my release. I understand the need to arrange follow-up care with the provider as indicated. I understand that I should
contact my primary care provider immediately or return to the Emergency Department, if my condition worsens, fails to improve, or new
symptoms appear.

If you need a printed copy of your medical records, call [PHONE-162] or go online at
JofLHealth.org/patients-visitors/medical-records-requests.
The examination and treatment you have received in the Emergency Department has been done to provide an appropriate evaluation
and stabilizing treatment on an emergency basis only. Given the limited resources, it is not meant to be a substitute for complete
medical care. The follow-up provider you named will receive a copy of your records and all test reports. IT IS IMPORTANT THAT YOU
SCHEDULE A FOLLOW-UP APPOINTMENT AND BE RE-EVALUATED. You should report any new complaints, symptoms, or
remaining problems at that time. IT IS IMPOSSIBLE FOR THE EMERGENCY DEPARTMENT TO RECOGNIZE AND TREAT ALL
ELEMENTS OF INJURY OR ILLNESS IN A SINGLE VISIT.
If you have been referred to a specialist provider, it means that we believe you may have a condition that requires the expertise of a
specialist. These providers work in partnership with the hospital and have agreed to see referred patients in their office for further
evaluation. KEEP IN MIND THAT THE SPECIALIST HAS HIS/HER OWN OFFICE POLICIES WHICH MAY REQUIRE PROPER
INSURANCE OR PAYMENT UP FRONT BEFORE THE SPECIALIST WILL SEE YOU. It is your responsibility to call the specialist
provider to make an appointment. We do not have the ability to refer patients to specialists/physicians that work with specific insurance
companies.
Please be advised that all financial charges or billing practices are determined by that practice, not the hospital. If your insurance
company requires that you see a specialist from their approved list, it is your responsibility to contact your insurance company to make
those arrangements. It is also your responsibility to follow any other requirements of your insurance company necessary to obtain
coverage for claims submitted.
I hereby acknowledge receipt of these instructions and information above. I understand that I have received Emergency Treatment only,
which is not a substitute for complete medical care and acknowledge that all of my medical problems may not be known, identified, or
treated prior to my release. I understand the need to arrange follow-up care with the provider as indicated. I understand that I should
contact my primary care provider immediately or return to the Emergency Department, if my condition worsens, fails to improve, or new
symptoms appear.

Coagulation
Collected Date
Collected Time
8/29/2023
22:07 EDT
Procedure Units Ref Range
PT 11.0#1 R1 Second(s) [9.7-11.5]
INR 1.0#2 R1
PTT 29.9#3 R1 Second(s) [23.3-33.2]
Interpretive Data
#1: PT
When using the PT to screen for a coagulopathy, please refer to the PT reference
range to evaluate results.
#2: INR
To monitor warfarin, the INR calculated from the PT is used, according to current
published guidelines:
*Most indications, moderate intensity INR (2.0-3.0) is effective.
*Patients with recurrent thromboembolic events with a therapeutic INR as above, or
other additional risk factors for thromboembolic events, high intensity INR
(2.5-3.5) is recommended.
*Optimal target range for the INR is not likely to be the same for all indications,
and lower INR targets may be prudent for patients at very high risk of bleeding.
The INR is used to manage patients on warfarin, and thus is not compared to a
"normal" INR range. The validity of the INR in other conditions of impaired
coagulation has not been fully evaluated, and the PT recorded in seconds is
recommended in these instances. Ref: CHEST June 2008 supplement.
#3: PTT
 
To screen for coagulaopathy, refer to reference range in seconds.
 
To monitor intravenous unfractionated heparin, the therapeutic aPTT range has been
determined by this laboratory to be 55.1 - 66.4 seconds. Patients who require high
doses of heparin to achieve a therapeutic aPTT, or in patients with a prolonged
baseline aPTT (ie lupus anticoagulant), it is reasonable to adjust heparin doses
based on anti Xa levels (unfractionated heparin assay) to achieve a level of 0.3 -
0.7 IU/ml. The aPTT is also used to monitor direct thrombin inhibitors as per
pharmacy protocols.
Performing Locations
R1: This test was performed at:
UofL Health - UofL Hospital, Pathology Department, 530 S. Jackson Street, Louisville, KY, 40202- ,
US, [PHONE-289]

USING AND SHARING MY INFORMATION
The Law: There is a federal law called the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of 1996
("HIPAA"). This law requires UofL Health to protect the privacy and security of its patients' treatment, contact,
and financial information. Taken together, this information is called your "Health Information". There are also
other federal and/or state laws that require UofL Health to take additional steps to protect certain categories of
Health Information including, but not limited to, Health Information about behavioral or mental health;
developmental disa ilities; treatment for substance abuse (alcohol and/or drugs) disorders; genetic testing and
counseling; HIV/AID'S sexual assault/ abuse; sexually transmitted illnesses; pregnancy; birth control; domestic
abuse of an adult with a disability; child abuse and neglect.
Authorization and Notice of Privacy Practices ("NPP"):If my permission is required by law, by signing this
form I agree that UCIL Health may receive, use and disclose my Health Information as set forth in this Consent
and as set forth in JofL Health's NPP. I understand that I can find more information about my rights to my
Health Information, and about how UofL Health uses my Health Information, in the NPP. I acknowledge that if I
requested a copy O the NPP that I have been given a copy. I further understand that the NPP is available on
UofL Health's website at: www.uoflhealth.org.
I agree that my pern ission applies to all of my Health Information in UofL Health's possession, including but not
limited to my contact information, problem list, diagnostic test results, medication list, allergy list, immunizations,
medical history, surgeries, procedures, and other clinically relevant data.
I understand that UcfL Health cannot control how others that receive my Health Information will protect or use
my information. I un erstand that others may not be required by law to protect my Health Information.
Purposes for which my Health Information may be shared: I understand that UofL Health may receive, use,
and disclose my Information for the purposes outlined in the NPP. In particular, UofL Health may use
and disclose my Hea th Information for the following purposes:
Data Sharing Program Purposes: I understand and agree that the use and disclosure of my health
information for certai aspects of treatment at UofL Health may be disclosed to other people involved with my
care outside UofL Halth. If I desire to revoke my consent, even in an emergency situation, I must notify UofL
Health's Health olimation Management Department by phone: [PHONE-325], option 2. I understand and
agree that my reques will be evaluated to determine if it is reasonable and in the best interest of my health care
to comply with my request. I will be notified in writing of as to whether UofL Health will be able to grant my
request. If my request is granted and I am are in need of emergency treatment, UofL Health may end the
restriction if the info mation is needed to provide my care. (See our Notice of Privacy Practices for more
information on these types of uses and disclosures for further information.)
Fundraising Activit es: UofL Health relies on fundraising to help support caring for all patients. I give my
permission to be con acted relating to fundraising opportunities. If I prefer not to be contacted about fundraising,
I must notify UofL Health by email to: [EMAIL-326] or by phone [PHONE-327]
Operational Purpos s: I agree that the contact information I give to UofL Health, such as telephone numbers
and email addresses may be used by UofL Health and third parties acting for UofL Health to communicate with
me for operational purposes including appointment reminders, follow up treatment reminders, flu shot
reminders, and patie surveys.

AUTHORIZATION OF REPRESENTATIVE TO APPEAL
I understand that Medicare and other payers do not pay the difference in the cost between a private and
semi-private room when use of a private room is not necessary for medical reasons. I hereby agree that the
difference in the cost between a semi-private and private room will be my responsibility to pay if I request one
at any point during my stay.
I hereby authorize and convey to UofL Health the full extent permissible under Federal and State law and under
any applicable insurance policy and/or employee health care benefit plan: (1) the right and ability to act as my
Authorized Representative in connection with any claim, right, matter, or cause of action that I may have under
such insurance policy and/or benefit plan; and (2) the right and ability to act as my Authorized Representative to
pursue such claim, right, matter, or cause of action in connection with said insurance policy and/or benefit plan,
including the right and ability to act as my Authorized Representative with respect to a benefit plan governed by
the provisions of the Employee Retirement Income Security Act ("ERISA").
I also authorize UofL Health to act on my behalf to (1) obtain copies of my insurance policy or benefit plan
documents from my insurer(s) or other Plan Administrator; (2) pursue appeals of adverse benefits decisións
claims for breaches of fiduciary duty under ERISA, external appeal review under Federal or State statute
administrative hearings, or legal actions to obtain payment from any payor; (3) disclose my protected health
information to my insurer(s), its affiliates, any plan fiduciary, or independent review organization that may be
involved in the resolution of claims, in connection with filing or appealing any claim for benefits due; and (4)
receive any notices in connection with my benefit claims or appeals concerning same.
If my admission to UofL Health is a result of a work-related injury, ] hereby waive any privilege ] may have with
UofL Health, or other healthcare provider, and [ hereby authorize these providers to provide the worker's
compensation administrator any information related to my injury or to my past relevant medical history. In the
event there is a dispute about the compensability of my claim or worker's compensation benefits, and if my
employer is not specifically determined by a Court of the Department of Labor to be responsible for worker's
compensation medical expenses for the condition or injury that is the basis of my admission, ] agree to be
personally responsible for all such expenses. ] further agree that, if my worker's compensation claim is settled
with my employer on a disputed basis without a specific finding that such is compensable as a worker's
compensation injury I (or my attorney, if [ am represented) will withhold sufficient funds from any settlement to
pay all amounts owed to UofL Health for treatment of the condition which is the basis for this admission, and
hereby grant an assignment to UofL Health for payment of all such expenses under such circumstances.

TREATMENT

performed by my ad nitting and treating physicians.

non-physician clinica students).

TESTING FOR INFECTIOUS DISEASES

Immunodeficiency Vrus ("HIV"), Hepatitis, or any other blood borne infectious disease as well COVID-19 or
any airborne pathog en if a physician or advanced practice registered nurse orders the test for diagnostic
purposes. I also understand that, in the case of exposure of a health care provider or first responder (such as

FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY

other sources.

Health or to the physcians providing Services at UofL Health. I understand they will bill my insurance directly
